      <p><b>Qatar</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span></span>/</a></span></span>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Qatar.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/29/En-us-Qatar.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Qatar.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ər/: 'er' in 'letter'">ər</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Qatar-2.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/09/En-us-Qatar-2.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Qatar-2.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">قطر</span>‎ <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Qaṭar</i></i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:IPA_for_Arabic" title="Wikipedia:IPA for Arabic">[ˈqɑtˤɑr]</a></span>; local vernacular pronunciation: <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:IPA_for_Arabic" title="Wikipedia:IPA for Arabic">[ɡɪtˤɑr]</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-EoI_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EoI-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> officially the <b>State of Qatar</b> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">دولة قطر</span>‎ <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">Dawlat Qaṭar</i></i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign</a> <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>. It is on the small Qatar Peninsula on the northeastern coast of the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a>. Its only land border is with <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> to the south, with the rest of its territory surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>. A strait in the Persian Gulf separates Qatar from the nearby island country of <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, as well as sharing <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maritime_border&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maritime border (not yet started)">maritime borders</a> with the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>. </p>
      <p>Following <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> rule, Qatar became a British protectorate in the early 20th century until gaining independence in 1971. Qatar has been ruled by the House of Thani since the early 19th century. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jassim_bin_Mohammed_Al_Thani&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jassim bin Mohammed Al Thani (not yet started)">Sheikh Jassim bin Mohammed Al Thani</a> was the founder of the State of Qatar. Qatar is a <a href="/wiki/Hereditary_monarchy" title="Hereditary monarchy">hereditary monarchy</a> and its head of state is Emir <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad_Al_Thani&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sheikh Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani (not yet started)">Sheikh Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani</a>. Whether it should be called a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional</a><sup id="cite_ref-BBC9Sep05_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC9Sep05-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USState2011_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USState2011-13">[13]</a></sup> or an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a><sup id="cite_ref-ftManage_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ftManage-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ciaw_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciaw-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cangov_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cangov-16">[16]</a></sup> is a matter of opinion. In 2003, the constitution was overwhelmingly approved in a referendum, with almost 98% in favour.<sup id="cite_ref-electionguide.org_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-electionguide.org-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-princeton.edu_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton.edu-18">[18]</a></sup> As of early 2017, Qatar's total population was around 2.6 million: 313,000 Qatari citizens and 2.3 million <a href="/w/index.php?title=Expatriates&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Expatriates (not yet started)">expatriates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar is a high income economy and is a developed country, with the world's third largest <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves (not yet started)">natural gas reserves</a> and oil reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The country has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">highest</a> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> in the world. Qatar is classified by the UN as a country of very high human development and is the most advanced Arab state for human development.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Qatar is a significant power in the Arab world, supporting several <a href="/wiki/Rebellion" title="Rebellion">rebel</a> groups during the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> both financially and through its globally expanding media group, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Jazeera_Media_Network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Jazeera Media Network (not yet started)">Al Jazeera Media Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> For its small size, Qatar has a lot of influence in the world, and has been identified as a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Middle_power&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Middle power (not yet started)">middle power</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Qatar will host the <a href="/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2022 FIFA World Cup">2022 FIFA World Cup</a>, becoming the first Arab country to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chuck_Hagel_meets_with_Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad,_Emir_of_Qatar,_December_2013_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Chuck_Hagel_meets_with_Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad%2C_Emir_of_Qatar%2C_December_2013_%281%29.jpg/220px-Chuck_Hagel_meets_with_Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad%2C_Emir_of_Qatar%2C_December_2013_%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Chuck_Hagel_meets_with_Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad%2C_Emir_of_Qatar%2C_December_2013_%281%29.jpg/330px-Chuck_Hagel_meets_with_Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad%2C_Emir_of_Qatar%2C_December_2013_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Chuck_Hagel_meets_with_Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad%2C_Emir_of_Qatar%2C_December_2013_%281%29.jpg/440px-Chuck_Hagel_meets_with_Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad%2C_Emir_of_Qatar%2C_December_2013_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3280"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chuck_Hagel_meets_with_Sheikh_Tamim_bin_Hamad,_Emir_of_Qatar,_December_2013_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Emir <a href="/wiki/Tamim_bin_Hamad_Al_Thani" title="Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani">Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani</a> with Former US Secretary of Defense <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Hagel" title="Chuck Hagel">Chuck Hagel</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Qatar is either a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional</a><sup id="cite_ref-BBC9Sep05_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC9Sep05-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USState2011_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USState2011-13">[13]</a></sup> or an <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolute monarchy</a><sup id="cite_ref-ftManage_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ftManage-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cangov_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cangov-16">[16]</a></sup> ruled by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Thani&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="House of Thani (not yet started)">Al Thani family</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> The Al Thani dynasty has been ruling Qatar since the family house was established in 1825.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> In 2003, Qatar adopted a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Constitution_of_Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Constitution of Qatar (not yet started)">constitution</a> that provided for the direct election of 30 of the 45 members of the Legislative Council.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lambert2011a_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert2011a-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reut20111101_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reut20111101-31">[31]</a></sup> The constitution was overwhelmingly approved in a referendum, with almost 98% in favour.<sup id="cite_ref-electionguide.org_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-electionguide.org-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-princeton.edu_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-princeton.edu-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The eighth Emir of Qatar is <a href="/wiki/Tamim_bin_Hamad_Al_Thani" title="Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani">Tamim bin Hamad Al Thani</a>, whose father <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Khalifa_Al_Thani" title="Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani">Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani</a> handed power to him on June 25, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Emir_BBC_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Emir_BBC-32">[32]</a></sup> The supreme chancellor has the exclusive power to appoint and remove the prime minister and cabinet ministers who, together, constitute the Council of Ministers, which is the supreme executive authority in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-embassycouncil_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embassycouncil-33">[33]</a></sup> The Council of Ministers also initiates legislation. Laws and decrees proposed by the Council of Ministers are referred to the Advisory Council (Majilis Al Shura) for discussion after which they are submitted to the Emir for ratification.<sup id="cite_ref-embassycouncil_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embassycouncil-33">[33]</a></sup> A <a href="/w/index.php?title=Consultative_Assembly_of_Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Consultative Assembly of Qatar (not yet started)">Consultative Assembly</a> has limited power to draft and approve laws, but the Emir has final say on all matters.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> The current Council is made up entirely of members appointed by the Emir,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> as no legislative elections have been held since 1970 when there were partial elections to the body.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Legislative elections are expected to be held in 2016.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">source?</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Qatari law does not permit the establishment of political bodies or trade unions.<sup id="cite_ref-kuwari_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kuwari-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sharia_law">Sharia law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=1" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Sharia law">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Change section: Sharia law">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">Sharia law</a> is the main source of Qatari legislation according to Qatar's Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-con_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-con-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qat1_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qat1-36">[36]</a></sup> In practice, Qatar's legal system is a mixture of <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil law (legal system)">civil law</a> and Sharia law.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Sharia law is applied to laws pertaining to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Family_law&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Family law (not yet started)">family law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inheritance" title="Inheritance">inheritance</a>, and several <a href="/wiki/Criminal_law" title="Criminal law">criminal acts</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Adultery" title="Adultery">adultery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robbery" title="Robbery">robbery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murder</a>). In some cases in Sharia-based <a href="/w/index.php?title=Family_court&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Family court (not yet started)">family courts</a>, a female's testimony is worth half a man's.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Codified family law was introduced in 2006. Islamic <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamy</a> is allowed in the country. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Flogging" title="Flogging">Flogging</a> is used in Qatar as a punishment for alcohol consumption or illicit sexual relations.<sup id="cite_ref-amne_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amne-40">[40]</a></sup> Article 88 of Qatar's criminal code declares the punishment for adultery is <a href="/wiki/Flagellation" class="mw-redirect" title="Flagellation">100 lashes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-flog_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flog-41">[41]</a></sup> In 2006, a <a href="/wiki/Filipino_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino people">Filipino</a> woman was sentenced to 100 lashes for adultery.<sup id="cite_ref-flog_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flog-41">[41]</a></sup> In 2010, at least 18 people (mostly foreign nationals) were sentenced to flogging of between 40 and 100 lashes for offences related to "illicit sexual relations" or alcohol consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In 2011, at least 21 people (mostly foreign nationals) were sentenced to floggings of between 30 and 100 lashes for offences related to "illicit sexual relations" or alcohol consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In 2012, six expatriates were sentenced to floggings of either 40 or 100 lashes.<sup id="cite_ref-amne_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amne-40">[40]</a></sup> Only Muslims considered medically fit were liable to have such sentences carried out. It is unknown if the sentences were implemented.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> More recently in April 2013, a Muslim expatriate was sentenced to 40 lashes for alcohol consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In June 2014, a Muslim expatriate was sentenced to 40 lashes for consuming alcohol and driving under the influence.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Judicial_corporal_punishment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Judicial corporal punishment (not yet started)">Judicial corporal punishment</a> is common in Qatar due to the <a href="/wiki/Hanbali" title="Hanbali">Hanbali interpretation</a> of Sharia Law. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Stoning" title="Stoning">Stoning</a> is a legal punishment in Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Apostasy" title="Apostasy">Apostasy</a> is a crime punishable by the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a> in Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-iheu_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iheu-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy" title="Blasphemy">Blasphemy</a> is punishable by up to seven years in prison and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Proselytizing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Proselytizing (not yet started)">proselytizing</a> can be punished by up to 10 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-iheu_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iheu-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">Homosexuality</a> is a crime punishable by the <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty" title="Death penalty">death penalty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverage">Alcohol</a> consumption is partially legal in Qatar; some five-star luxury hotels are allowed to sell alcohol to their non-Muslim customers.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj20120107_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj20120107-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arabist20120115_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arabist20120115-53">[53]</a></sup> Muslims are not allowed to consume alcohol in Qatar and Muslims caught consuming alcohol are liable to <a href="/wiki/Flogging" title="Flogging">flogging</a> or deportation. Non-Muslim expatriates can obtain a permit to purchase alcohol for personal consumption. The Qatar Distribution Company (a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a>) is permitted to import alcohol and pork; it operates the one and only liquor store in the country, which also sells pork to holders of liquor licences.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Qatari officials have also indicated a willingness to allow alcohol in "fan zones" at the <a href="/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2022 FIFA World Cup">2022 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until recently, restaurants on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Pearl-Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Pearl-Qatar (not yet started)">Pearl-Qatar</a> (a man-made island near Doha) were allowed to serve alcoholic drinks.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj20120107_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj20120107-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arabist20120115_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arabist20120115-53">[53]</a></sup> In December 2011, however, restaurants on the Pearl were told to stop selling alcohol.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj20120107_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj20120107-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-er6012012_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-er6012012-57">[57]</a></sup> No explanation was given for the ban.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj20120107_52-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj20120107-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arabist20120115_53-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arabist20120115-53">[53]</a></sup> Speculation about the reason includes the government's desire to project a more pious image in advance of the country's first election of a royal advisory body and rumours of a financial dispute between the government and the resort's developers.<sup id="cite_ref-er6012012_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-er6012012-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, Qatar launched a modesty campaign to remind tourists of the modest dress code.<sup id="cite_ref-'Leggings_Are_Not_Pants'_Qatar's_New_Modesty_Campaign_Aimed_At_Westerners_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-'Leggings_Are_Not_Pants'_Qatar's_New_Modesty_Campaign_Aimed_At_Westerners-58">[58]</a></sup> Female tourists are advised not to wear leggings, miniskirts, sleeveless dresses and short or tight clothing in public. Men are advised against wearing only shorts and singlets.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=2" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Human rights">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Change section: Human rights">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_rights_in_Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Human rights in Qatar (not yet started)">Human rights in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/U.S._State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. State Department">U.S. State Department</a>, expatriate workers from nations throughout <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> voluntarily migrate to Qatar as low-skilled laborers or domestic servants, but some subsequently face conditions indicative of involuntary servitude. Some of the more common labor rights violations include beatings, withholding of payment, charging workers for benefits for which the employer is responsible, restrictions on freedom of movement (such as the confiscation of passports, travel documents, or exit permits), arbitrary detention, threats of legal action, and sexual assault.<sup id="cite_ref-2011narrq_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011narrq-60">[60]</a></sup> Many migrant workers arriving for work in Qatar have paid exorbitant fees to recruiters in their home countries.<sup id="cite_ref-2011narrq_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011narrq-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2014, certain provisions of the Qatari Criminal Code allows punishments such as <a href="/wiki/Flogging" title="Flogging">flogging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stoning" title="Stoning">stoning</a> to be imposed as criminal sanctions. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=UN_Committee_Against_Torture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="UN Committee Against Torture (not yet started)">UN Committee Against Torture</a> found that these practices constituted a breach of the obligations imposed by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=United_Nations_Convention_Against_Torture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="United Nations Convention Against Torture (not yet started)">UN Convention Against Torture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Qatar retains the death penalty, mainly for threats against national security. Use of the death penalty is rare and no state executions have taken place in Qatar since 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under the provisions of Qatar's sponsorship law, sponsors have the unilateral power to cancel workers' residency permits, deny workers' ability to change employers, report a worker as "absconded" to police authorities, and deny permission to leave the country.<sup id="cite_ref-2011narrq_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011narrq-60">[60]</a></sup> As a result, sponsors may restrict workers' movements and workers may be afraid to report abuses or claim their rights.<sup id="cite_ref-2011narrq_60-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011narrq-60">[60]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/w/index.php?title=ITUC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ITUC (not yet started)">ITUC</a>, the visa sponsorship system allows the exaction of <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour" class="mw-redirect" title="Forced labour">forced labour</a> by making it difficult for a migrant worker to leave an abusive employer or travel overseas without permission.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Qatar also does not maintain wage standards for its <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrant</a> labourers. Qatar commissioned international law firm <a href="/w/index.php?title=DLA_Piper&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="DLA Piper (not yet started)">DLA Piper</a> to produce a report investigating the immigrant labour system. In May 2014 DLA Piper released over 60 recommendations for reforming the kafala system including the abolition of exit visas and the introduction of a minimum wage which Qatar has pledged to implement.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 2012, Qatari officials declared their intention to allow the establishment of an independent trade union.<sup id="cite_ref-unions_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unions-66">[66]</a></sup> Qatar also announced it will scrap its sponsor system for foreign labour, which requires that all foreign workers be sponsored by local employers.<sup id="cite_ref-unions_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unions-66">[66]</a></sup> Additional changes to labour laws include a provision guaranteeing that all workers' salaries are paid directly into their bank accounts and new restrictions on working outdoors in the hottest hours during the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> New draft legislation announced in early 2015 mandates that companies that fail to pay workers' wages on time could temporarily lose their ability to hire more employees.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2015 Qatar's Emir signed into law new reforms to the country's sponsorship system, with the new law taking effect within one year.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Critics claim that the changes could fail to address some labour rights issues.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country enfranchised women at the same time as men in connection with the 1999 elections for a Central Municipal Council.<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert2011a_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert2011a-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> These elections—the first ever in Qatar—were deliberately held on March 8, 1999, <a href="/wiki/International_Women%27s_Day" title="International Women's Day">International Women's Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert2011a_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert2011a-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=3" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Foreign relations">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Change section: Foreign relations">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Foreign_relations_of_Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Foreign relations of Qatar (not yet started)">Foreign relations of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Amir_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_al-Thani.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Amir_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_al-Thani.jpg/220px-Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Amir_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_al-Thani.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Amir_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_al-Thani.jpg/330px-Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Amir_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_al-Thani.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Amir_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_al-Thani.jpg/440px-Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Amir_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_al-Thani.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4003" data-file-height="2663"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Kerry_Meets_With_Amir_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_al-Thani.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Former Emir <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Khalifa_Al_Thani" title="Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani">Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani</a> and US Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> in 2013.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As a small country with larger neighbors, Qatar seeks to project influence and protect its state and ruling dynasty.<sup id="cite_ref-Boghardt_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boghardt-74">[74]</a></sup> The history of Qatar's alliances provides insight into the basis of their policy. Between 1760 and 1971, Qatar sought formal protection from the high transitory powers of the Ottomans, British, the Al-Khalifa's from Bahrain, the Arabians, and the <a href="/wiki/Wahhabi" title="Wahhabi">Wahhabis</a> from Saudi Arabia.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears (June 2013)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Qatar's rising international profile and active role in international affairs has led some analysts to identify it as a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Middle_power&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Middle power (not yet started)">middle power</a>. Qatar was an early member of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> and a founding member of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gulf_Cooperation_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gulf Cooperation Council (not yet started)">Gulf Cooperation Council</a> (GCC). It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>. The country has not accepted compulsory <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> jurisdiction.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar also has bilateral relationships with a variety of foreign powers. Qatar hosts the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Udeid_Air_Base&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Udeid Air Base (not yet started)">Al Udeid Air Base</a>, a joint U.S.-British base, which acts as the hub for all American and British air operations in the Persian Gulf.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> It has allowed American and British forces to use an air base to send supplies to Iraq and Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Despite hosting this strategic military installation, Qatar is not always a strong Western ally. Qatar has allowed the Afghan <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> to set up a political office inside the country and has close ties to Iran, including a shared natural gas field.<sup id="cite_ref-NRPpunch_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRPpunch-78">[78]</a></sup> According to leaked documents published in <i>The New York Times</i>, Qatar's record of counter-terrorism efforts was the "worst in the region".<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20130630_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20130630-79">[79]</a></sup> The cable suggested that Qatar's security service was "hesitant to act against known terrorists out of concern for appearing to be aligned with the U.S. and provoking reprisals".<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20130630_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20130630-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar has mixed relations with its neighbors in the Persian Gulf region. Qatar signed a defence co-operation agreement with Iran,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> with whom it shares the largest single non-associated gas field in the world. It was the second nation, the first being France, to have publicly announced its recognition of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Libyan_opposition&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Libyan opposition (not yet started)">Libyan opposition</a>'s <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_Transitional_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National Transitional Council (not yet started)">National Transitional Council</a> as the legitimate <a href="/w/index.php?title=Government_of_Libya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Government of Libya (not yet started)">government</a> of <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> amidst the <a href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_civil_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Libyan civil war">2011 Libyan civil war</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, Qatar's relations with <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> came to a boiling point over Qatar's support for the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood" title="Muslim Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a> and extremist groups in Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> This culminated in the three aforementioned countries withdrawing their ambassadors from Qatar in March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Islam_Hassan_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Islam_Hassan-83">[83]</a></sup> When the ambassadors withdrew, the GCC was reportedly on the verge of a crisis linked to the emergence of distinct political blocs with conflicting interests. Saudi Arabia, the UAE and Bahrain were engaged in a political struggle with Qatar, while Oman and Kuwait represent a non-aligned bloc within the GCC.<sup id="cite_ref-Islam_Hassan_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Islam_Hassan-83">[83]</a></sup> Relations between the countries improved after the Gulf Cooperation Council (GCC) announced Bahrain, Saudi Arabia, and the UAE returned their diplomats to Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> Islam Hassan, a researcher in Persian Gulf Studies at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Qatar University (not yet started)">Qatar University</a>, claims that, with the resolution of the GCC crisis, Qatar reached a new level of political maturity. He goes on to assert that Qatar managed to bring an end to the crisis without changing any of its foreign policy principles or abandoning its allies.<sup id="cite_ref-Islam_Hassan_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Islam_Hassan-83">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Qatar_in_Libya.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Qatar_in_Libya.jpg/220px-Flag_of_Qatar_in_Libya.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Qatar_in_Libya.jpg/330px-Flag_of_Qatar_in_Libya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Flag_of_Qatar_in_Libya.jpg/440px-Flag_of_Qatar_in_Libya.jpg 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Qatar_in_Libya.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Qatar's flag in <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> after the <a href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Libyan Civil War">Libyan Civil War</a>; Qatar played an influential role during the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In recent years, Qatar has been using Islamist militants in a number of countries including Egypt, Syria, Libya, Somalia and Mali to further its foreign policy. Courting Islamists from the Muslim Brotherhood to <a href="/w/index.php?title=Salafi_movement&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Salafi movement (not yet started)">Salafist</a> groups has served as a power amplifier for the country, as it believes since the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> that these groups represented the wave of the future.<sup id="cite_ref-Boghardt_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boghardt-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt20130630_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20130630-79">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> David Cohen, the Under Secretary for terrorism and financial intelligence at the U.S. Treasury, said that Qatar is a "permissive jurisdiction for terrorist financing."<sup id="cite_ref-ISIS_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISIS-86">[86]</a></sup> There is evidence that these groups supported by Qatar include the hard-line Islamic militant groups active in northern Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt20130630_79-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20130630-79">[79]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://simple.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Qatar, Saudi Arabia and Turkey are openly backing the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Army_of_Conquest&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Army of Conquest (not yet started)">Army of Conquest</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> an umbrella group of anti-government forces fighting in the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a> that reportedly includes an <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> linked <a href="/wiki/Al-Nusra_Front" title="Al-Nusra Front">al-Nusra Front</a> and another <a href="/w/index.php?title=Salafi_jihadism&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Salafi jihadism (not yet started)">Salafi</a> coalition known as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ahrar_ash-Sham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ahrar ash-Sham (not yet started)">Ahrar ash-Sham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ISIS_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISIS-86">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar supported the democratically elected President <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Morsi" title="Mohamed Morsi">Mohamed Morsi</a> with diplomatic support and the state-owned <a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Jazeera_network&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Jazeera network (not yet started)">Al Jazeera network</a> before he was deposed in a military coup.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FP_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FP-91">[91]</a></sup> Qatar offered Egypt a $7.5 billion loan during the year he was in power.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar's alignment with <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>, first reported in early 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-bbchamas_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbchamas-93">[93]</a></sup> has drawn criticism from Israel, the United States, Egypt and Saudi Arabia, "who accuse Qatar of undermining regional stability by supporting Hamas."<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> However, the Foreign Minister of Qatar has denied supporting Hamas, stating "We do not support Hamas but we support the Palestinians."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Following a peace agreement, Qatar pledged $1 billion in humanitarian aid to Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar has hosted academic, religious, political, and economic conferences. The 11th annual Doha Forum recently brought in key thinkers, professionals of various backgrounds, and political figures from all over the world to discuss democracy, media and information technology, free trade, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_security&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Water security (not yet started)">water security</a> issues. In addition, the forum has featured the Middle East Economic Future conference since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In more recent times, Qatar has hosted peace talks between rival factions across the globe. Notable among these include the Darfur Agreement. The Doha Declaration is the basis of the peace process in Darfur and it has achieved significant gains on the ground for the African region. Notable achievements included the restoration of security and stability, progress made in construction and reconstruction processes, return of displaced residents and uniting of Darfur people to face challenges and push forward the peace process.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Qatar donated £88.5million in funds to finance recovery and reconstruction in Darfur.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=4" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Military">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Change section: Military">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar_Armed_Forces&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Qatar Armed Forces (not yet started)">Qatar Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2170" data-file-height="1346"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Qatar's <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_2000" title="Dassault Mirage 2000">Dassault Mirage 2000</a> flying over <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Qatar Armed Forces are the military forces of Qatar. The country maintains a modest military force of approximately 11,800 men, including an army (8,500), navy (1,800) and air force (1,500). Qatar's defence expenditures accounted for approximately 4.2% of gross national product in 1993. In 2008 Qatar spent US$2.355 billion on military expenditures, 2.3% of the gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Qatari special forces have been trained by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and other Western countries, and are believed to possess considerable skill.<sup id="cite_ref-strangepow_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strangepow-101">[101]</a></sup> They also helped the Libyan rebels during the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Battle_of_Tripoli_(2011)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Battle of Tripoli (2011) (not yet started)">2011 Battle of Tripoli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-strangepow_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strangepow-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar has signed defence pacts with the United States and United Kingdom, as well as with France earlier in 1994. Qatar plays an active role in the collective defence efforts of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf (not yet started)">Gulf Cooperation Council</a>; the other five members are Saudi Arabia, Kuwait, Bahrain, the UAE, and Oman. The presence of a large Qatari Air Base, operated by the United States and several other UN nations, provides a guaranteed source of defence and national security. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stockholm International Peace Research Institute (not yet started)">Stockholm International Peace Research Institute</a>, SIPRI, found that in 2010–14 Qatar was the 46th largest arms importer in the world. However, SIPRI writes, Qatar's plans to transform and significantly enlarge its armed forces have accelerated. Orders in 2013 for 62 tanks and 24 self-propelled guns from Germany were followed in 2014 by a number of other contracts, including 24 combat helicopters and 3 AEW aircraft from the USA, and 2 tanker aircraft from Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar's military participated in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen (not yet started)">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Houthis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Houthis (not yet started)">Houthis</a>. In 2015, <i>Al Jazeera America</i> reported: "Numerous reports suggest that the Saudi-led coalition against opposition groups in Yemen has indiscriminately attacked civilians and used cluster bombs in civilian-populated areas, in violation of international law."<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=5" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Administrative divisions">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Change section: Administrative divisions">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Qatar,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/250px-Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/375px-Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg/500px-Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1039" data-file-height="987"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Qatar,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Municipalities of Qatar since 2004
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Municipalities_of_Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Municipalities of Qatar (not yet started)">Municipalities of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 2004, Qatar has been divided into seven municipalities (Arabic: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baladiyah&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Baladiyah (not yet started)">baladiyah</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ol>
       <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madinat_ash_Shamal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Madinat ash Shamal (not yet started)">Madinat ash Shamal</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Khor_(municipality)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Khor (municipality) (not yet started)">Al Khor</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Umm_Salal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Umm Salal (not yet started)">Umm Salal</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Daayen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Daayen (not yet started)">Al Daayen</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Rayyan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Rayyan (not yet started)">Al Rayyan</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Wakrah" title="Al Wakrah">Al Wakrah</a></li>
      </ol> 
      <p>For statistical purposes, the municipalities are further subdivided into 98 zones (as of 2010<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://simple.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>),<sup id="cite_ref-admdiv_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admdiv-105">[105]</a></sup> which are in turn subdivided into blocks.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=6" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Geography">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Change section: Geography">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Qatar is a <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> (a strip of land sticking out into the sea). It is joined to <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> to the south, and all the other sides of it are surrounded by the waters of the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Gulf" class="mw-disambig" title="Arabian Gulf">Arabian Gulf</a>. </p>
      <p>Qatar is quite a small country and has an area of only 10,360&nbsp;km². The peninsula is 160&nbsp;km long. Much of the country is a low, barren <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plain</a>, covered with <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a>. The Jebel Dukhan area has Qatar’s main onshore <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" title="Oil field">oil deposits</a>. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Natural_gas_field&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Natural gas field (not yet started)">natural gas fields</a> lie offshore, to the northwest of the peninsula. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Capital_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital (city)">capital</a> of Qatar is <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>. Over 90% of the people live in Doha. The other large city is <a href="/wiki/Al_Wakrah" title="Al Wakrah">Al Wakrah</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=7" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Government and politics">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Change section: Government and politics">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Qatar has an unelected, monarchic, <a href="/wiki/Emirate" title="Emirate">emirate</a>-type government. The position of emir is <a href="/wiki/Hereditary" class="mw-redirect" title="Hereditary">hereditary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Emir is the only one who can appoint and remove the prime minister and cabinet ministers. Together the ministers make up the Council of Ministers. They are the highest executive authority in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-qatarembassy_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qatarembassy-107">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="People_and_culture">People and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=8" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: People and culture">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Change section: People and culture">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>People from Qatar are called <b>Qataris</b>. They are <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arabs</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Qatar is <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, but many people also speak <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, especially when they are doing <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">business</a>. </p>
      <p>About 2.6 million people live in Qatar; however, about 88% of these are <i>guest workers</i> (people from another country who are living and working there for a short time), mostly coming from South Asia, South East Asia and other Arab countries. 650,000 are Indians, 350,000 Nepalis, 260,000 Filipinos among a lot of other nationalities.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nearly all of Qatar's economy comes from producing <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">petroleum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currency</a> of Qatar is called the <b>Qatari Riyal</b>. </p>
      <p>Almost all Qataris follow the <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. However, many of the guest workers follow other religions. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=9" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: Sport">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Change section: Sport">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Qatar, closely followed by <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>. The Qatar under-20 national football team finished second in the <a href="/w/index.php?title=1981_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1981 FIFA World Youth Championship (not yet started)">1981 FIFA World Youth Championship</a>. </p>
      <p>The Asian Football Confederation's <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_AFC_Asian_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2011 AFC Asian Cup (not yet started)">2011 AFC Asian Cup</a> finals were held in Qatar in January 2011. It was the second time it has been hosted by Qatar, the other being the <a href="/w/index.php?title=1988_AFC_Asian_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1988 AFC Asian Cup (not yet started)">1988 AFC Asian Cup</a>. </p>
      <p>Doha, Qatar, is also home to Qatar Racing Club a <a href="/wiki/Drag_Racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Drag Racing">Drag Racing</a> facility. </p>
      <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Khalifa_International_Tennis_and_Squash_Complex&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Khalifa International Tennis and Squash Complex (not yet started)">Khalifa International Tennis and Squash Complex</a> in Doha, Qatar, hosted the <a href="/w/index.php?title=WTA_Tour_Championships&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="WTA Tour Championships (not yet started)">WTA Tour Championships</a> in women's tennis between 2008 and 2010. Doha holds the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women's Tennis Association">WTA</a> Premier tournament <a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar_Ladies_Open&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Qatar Ladies Open (not yet started)">Qatar Ladies Open</a> each year. </p>
      <p>On December 2, 2010, Qatar won their bid to host the <a href="/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2022 FIFA World Cup">2022 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nasser_Al-Attiyah&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nasser Al-Attiyah (not yet started)">Nasser Al-Attiyah</a> of Qatar won the <a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Dakar_Rally&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2011 Dakar Rally (not yet started)">2011 Dakar Rally</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Production_World_Rally_Championship&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Production World Rally Championship (not yet started)">Production World Rally Championship</a> in 2006. In addition, he has also won gold medals at the <a href="/w/index.php?title=2002_Asian_Games&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="2002 Asian Games (not yet started)">2002 Asian Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/2010_Asian_Games" title="2010 Asian Games">2010 Asian Games</a> as part of the Qatari <a href="/w/index.php?title=Skeet_shooting&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Skeet shooting (not yet started)">skeet shooting</a> team. </p>
      <p>Since 2002, Qatar has hosted the yearly <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tour_of_Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tour of Qatar (not yet started)">Tour of Qatar</a>, a cycling race in six stages. Every February, riders are racing on the roads across Qatar's flat land for six days. Each stage covers a distance of more than 100&nbsp;km.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;veaction=edit&amp;section=10" class="mw-editsection-visualeditor" title="Change section: References">change</a><span class="mw-editsection-divider"> | </span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Change section: References">change source</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">October 7,</span> 2014</span>. <q>Two overarching goals have driven Qatari policy. One has been to maximize Qatar's influence on the regional and international stage. This originally reflected the personal ambition of the former ruler and current emir's father, Shaykh Hamad bin Khalifa al Thani, and his foreign minister and eventual prime minister, Shaykh Hamad bin Jassim al Thani.
